Each child must be provided with their own mat, pad, bed, or cot. 
5. 
The aisles between rows of cots, beds, or bunks must be kept clear for 
exiting purposes. There must be at least two (2) feet of clear space 
separating sides of cots, beds, or bunks. 
6. 
If bunk beds are in use, no bunks may contain more than two tiers of 
beds. There must be at least twenty-seven (27) inches of clear space 
separating the tiers of beds and thirty-six (36) inches of clear space 
between the top tier and the ceiling. Electric lights which are within reach 
of the top bunk must be protected. 
7. 
Each permanent sleeping unit, building, or tent must have at least thirty 
(30) square feet of floor space per person, child, or staff member for 
single-tier beds and twenty (20) square feet per person, child, or staff 
member for two (2) tier bunks. 
8. 
In tent structures which have a platform floor, beds or bunks must be 
arranged in such a fashion that no child who might fall from a bed or bunk 
could fall through the sides of the tent to the ground below. 
9. 
Campers must sleep in the same room or tent with individuals that are 
consistent with their gender identity. This rule is intended to mirror the 
requirements of the Colorado Anti-Discrimination Act (CADA), for places 
of public accommodation, sections 24-34-600.3 through 24-34-605, 
C.R.S., and its implementing regulations at 3 CCR 708-1. Rule 81.9 
(December 30, 2023), as incorporated by reference in section 2.235(D)(1). 
The Department does not provide advisory opinions about whether an 
entity is covered by CADA. 
2.600 RULES REGULATING SPECIAL ACTIVITIES 
2.601 AUTHORITY 
These rules and regulations are adopted pursuant to the rulemaking authority provided 
in section 26.5-1-105(1), C.R.S., and are intended to be consistent with the 
requirements of the State Administrative Procedures Act, sections 24-4-101 through 24-
4-204 (the “APA”), C.R.S., the Anna Jo Garcia Haynes Early Childhood Act, sections 
26.5-1-101 through 26.5-6-103 (the “Early Childhood Act”), C.R.S., the Child Care 
Licensing Act, sections 26.5-5-301 through 26.5-5-329, C.R.S.; and the Child Care 
Development and Block Grant Act of 2014, 42 U.S.C. sec. 9858e. 
The specific rulemaking authorities granted for Special Activities include section 26.5-5-
314, C.R.S.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
302 
2.602 SCOPE AND PURPOSE 
These rules and regulations shall govern the processes and procedures to become a 
licensed child care facility, and the health and safety requirements of licensed child care 
facilities in Colorado. These rules and regulations shall govern the health and safety 
requirements for special activities including Swimming, shoreline and wading activities, 
watercraft on flatwater, watercrafts on class I or class II moving water, white water 
rafting on class III and above, archery, riflery, ax-throwing, use of knives, horseback 
riding, rock climbing and climbing walls, single and or multi pitch climbing, high and or 
low ropes challenge courses, hiking, backpacking and camping, biking on public roads 
or mountain trails. 
2.603 APPLICABILITY 
The provisions of these rules and regulations shall be applicable to licensed child care 
providers participating in special activities, which include licensed School Age Child 
Care, Child Care Centers, Family Child Care Homes, and Children’s Resident Camps. 
2.604 DEFINITIONS 
A. 
“Action” means the functional mechanism that loads, fires, and ejects ammunition 
from a firearm. 
B. 
“Auto Belay” means an automatic electro-mechanical or mechanical climbing 
belay system. It replaces the need for a human belayer as the auto-belay 
automatically retracts the climbing rope, taking up the slack as you climb. A 
qualified individual must monitor the auto-belay system and attached climber. 
C. 
“Ax” means an ax or hatchet tool that consists of a heavy edged head attached to 
a handle. 
D. 
“Backstop or bullet stop” means a device, raised mound of earth, or suitable 
natural feature behind the targets, which is designed to safely capture fired 
bullets and constructed of material that prevents projectile ricochet. 
E. 
“Biking” means bicycling on a non-motorized bicycle. 
F. 
“Bouldering” is a form of free climbing that is performed on small rock formations 
or artificial rock walls without the use of ropes or harnesses. Bouldering under six 
(6) feet in height must follow all Playground Safety Regulations as listed in rule 
sections 2.230(C) of the rules regulating Child Care Centers, 2.337(B) of the 
rules regulating Family Child Care Homes, 2.424(G) of the rules regulating 
Children’s Resident Camps, and 2.524(A) of the rules regulating School-Age 
Child Care Centers.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
303 
1. 
Or the program must submit a written plan for Department approval as stated in 
this rule section 2.605(D). Bouldering over six (6) feet in height must follow all 
regulations as listed in rule section 2.618, or the program must submit a written 
plan for Department approval as stated in this rule section 2.605(D).  
G. 
“Class I moving water” means fast-moving water with small waves and riffles. 
H. 
“Class II moving water” means water that has medium-sized waves and some 
minor rocks or other obstacles. The water moves fast enough to create 
whitecaps that are one to three (1–3) feet high. 
I. 
“Firing distance” means the distance between the firing line and the target line. 
J. 
“Firing line” means a line parallel to the targets, from behind which firearms are 
discharged. 
K. 
“Firing point” means specific locations from which individual participants engage 
their targets. 
L. 
“Flat Water” means calm, level, or a slow-flowing water channel. 
M. 
“Hiking” means walking outdoors on a trail, or off trail, for recreational purposes 
may entail various, uphill, or downhill or rough terrains and may require more 
equipment preparedness and ability. 
N. 
“Nocking an arrow” means to fit (an arrow) against the bowstring. 
O. 
“Target line” means a line parallel to the firing line along which targets are 
placed. 
P. 
“Top rope climbing” means a style of climbing where the rope runs from the 
climber's harness up to an anchor system at the top of the route and back down 
to the belayer on the ground. This creates a continuous loop that protects the 
climber in case of a fall. 
Q. 
“Watercraft” means non-motorized vessels including sailboat(s), paddleboat(s), 
paddleboard(s), canoe(s), kayak(s), rowboat(s), float tube(s), and rafts. 
2.605 GENERAL PROVISIONS 
A. 
All activities must operate under the applicable federal, state, and local laws, 
codes, and regulations. Programs must obtain all required permits and licenses 
in the location where the activities are taking place. Documentation of permits 
and licenses must be available for the Department to review.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
304 
B. 
There shall be written policies and procedures that reflects the purpose of the 
program, including a list of activities. The policies and procedures must be 
provided to parents or guardians. 
C. 
Parents must be given the opportunity to indicate to a program whether they do 
not want their child to participate in a special activity. 
D. 
If the program participates in special activities other than those for which rules 
are found in this rule section, the program must submit a written plan to the 
Department for review prior to participating in the activity. The plan must include 
at least, the following: 
1. 
The qualifications of the instructor as applicable to the activity; 
2. 
The qualifications, of any other staff members or activity leaders 
participating in the activity; 
3. 
The number of necessary staff members and supervision of children 
participating in the activity; 
4. 
The number of children allowed to participate in the activity; 
5. 
The staff-to-child ratios and group size of children participating in the 
activity; 
6. 
Conditions under which a child may participate in the activity, such as age 
or skill level of the child; 
7. 
Any special equipment necessary, how the equipment will be stored, 
maintained, inspected, and replaced as needed. 
8. 
Access to medical treatment; 
9. 
Development of an emergency plan; 
10. 
Age and developmentally appropriate safety considerations; and 
11. 
Geographic location of where the activity will take place. 
E. 
Paint ball activities where children shoot paint balls at other children are 
prohibited. 
F. 
The instructor for each special activity must be at least eighteen (18) years of 
age (unless otherwise defined in this rule section and is responsible for 
overseeing the special activity, as well as setting standards for the selection and 
training of activity leaders and staff. 
1. 
The qualified instructor of each special activity must:

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
305 
a.  
Provide annual training and orientation for all staff participating in 
the activity in the operating, safety, emergency, and supervision 
procedures of the activity. 
1. 
Documentation of training must include the following: 
(a) 
Title of training. 
(b) 
Date and clock hours of training. 
(c) 
The name or signature of the trainer, or other 
approved method of verifying the identity of trainer or 
entity. 
b. 
Assign duties to activity leaders and staff members. 
c. 
Assure that all necessary equipment is complete, in good repair, 
and safe to use. 
d. 
Assure that environmental hazards are not severe enough to cause 
danger to children. 
G. 
Safety plans and rules shall be reviewed with participants at the beginning of 
each activity. 
H. 
All staff must be familiar with safety plans and rules for each activity they will be 
supervising. 
I. 
First Aid supplies shall be available at each special activity. The contents of each 
kit shall be adequate for the number of children and appropriate for the type of 
activity. 
J. 
The staff to child ratio for each type of program must be followed according to 
rules for that license type unless the ratio is different for the specified activity, in 
which case the activity staff to child ratio should apply. See rule sections 2.500 
regulating School-Age Care Centers, 2.200 regulating Child Care Centers, 2.400 
regulating Children’s Resident Camps, and 2.300 regulating Family Child Care 
Homes. 
K. 
There must be a staff member with current Department-approved First Aid and 
CPR training at each activity location. 
1. 
If any activity is more than thirty (30) minutes from emergency medical 
services, at least one (1) staff member with the group must hold a current 
Wilderness First aid Training certification.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
306 
L. 
If a child requires medication while away from the program, there must be at 
least one (1) staff member present with the group with current Department-
approved medication administration training who has been delegated by a 
registered nurse or physician to administer medications. The program must not 
exclude children with health conditions requiring medications from participating in 
these activities. 
1. 
For family child care homes participating in special activities rule section 
2.321(C)(2) regarding medication administration and mediation delegation 
apply. 
M. 
No child shall be forced to participate in any activity. 
N. 
If children are participating in multiple activities, rules regulating the specific 
special activity apply. 
O. 
The program must have a plan to address emergency situations while 
participating in the activity. 
P. 
A qualified staff member must be present supervising observers at the activity 
site and maintaining the ratios as defined at the specific ruleset the program is 
licensed as. 
Q. 
For all water activities, the program must have life-saving equipment that is 
readily accessible during water activities if a pool or body of water is six (6) feet 
or more in any direction and two (2) feet or more in depth. Life-saving equipment 
may include a ring buoy and rope, a rescue tube, a throwing line, and a 
shepherd's hook or reach pole that will not conduct electricity. 
R. 
Targets in archery, riflery, or ax throwing cannot be of the silhouette type or 
depict human form. 
WATER ACTIVITIES 
2.606 SWIMMING 
If Family Child Care Homes, Child Care Centers, School-Age Child Care Centers, 
Children’s Resident Camps, or Neighborhood Youth Organizations offer swimming 
activities, the following rules must be complied with: 
A. 
Qualifications: 
1. 
The swimming instructor must meet the following qualifications: 
a. 
Hold a current Red Cross lifeguard training certificate or equivalent 
training certificate from a nationally recognized organization.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
307 
b. 
Ten (10) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge 
and skill in lifeguarding. 
c. 
If the childcare program is offering swimming instruction, the 
swimming instructor must hold a current Red Cross water safety 
instructor certificate or equivalent certificate from a nationally 
recognized organization. 
2. 
Swimming activity leaders must be at least eighteen (18) years of age and 
meet the following qualifications: 
a. 
Hold a current Red Cross lifeguard training certificate or equivalent 
certificate from a nationally recognized organization; and, 
b. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by a 
swimming instructor. 
B. 
At any time the swimming area is open, there must be an individual with a current 
Red Cross lifeguard training certificate or equivalent training certificate from a 
nationally recognized organization present at the swimming area for each thirty 
(30) children in the water. 
C. 
The staff-to-child ratio while swimming must be one to ten (1:10). 
1. 
The swimming instructor or activity leaders do not count in the staff-to-
child ratio for supervision of children. 
D. 
The swimming area must be off limits when the swimming instructor or swimming 
activity leaders are not present. 
E. 
If the program uses a pool for which they are not responsible, the program must 
provide a qualified lifeguard if the pool does not provide one. 
F. 
Swimming area rules and emergency procedures must be posted in a visible 
location at the swimming area. 
G. 
The swimming pool or swimming area shall meet the standards of the Colorado 
Department of Public Health and Environment (CDPHE), as defined in 5 CCR 
1003-5 (December 15, 2020), herein incorporated by reference. No later editions 
or amendments are incorporated. These regulations are available from the 
Colorado Department of Public Health and Environment at no cost at 
https://www.coloradosos.gov/CCR/GenerateRulePdf.do?ruleVersionId=9173&file
Name=5%20CCR%201003-5. These recommendations are also available for 
public inspection and copying at the Colorado Department of Early Childhood, 
710 S. Ash St., Denver, CO 80246, during regular business hours. 
H. 
If children are permitted to swim in a lake or pond, swimming areas must be 
clearly designated.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
308 
I. 
Before children are permitted to swim in deep water, swimming skills must be 
tested by properly trained swimming activity leaders. 
J. 
There shall be a system known to children and staff for counting and supervising 
the children when children are in the water. 
K. 
The following equipment must be available for use at the pool side or the lake 
shore in which swimming is permitted: 
1. 
A rescue tube; 
2. 
Reach pole; and 
3. 
Backboard. 
2.607 SHORELINE AND WADING ACTIVITIES 
If Family Child Care Homes, Child Care Centers, School-Age Child Care Centers, 
Children’s Resident Camps, or Neighborhood Youth Organizations offer shoreline and 
wading activities, the following rules must be complied with: 
A. 
If a program has shoreline activities such as wading, fishing, ecology or nature 
studies, the program must have written policies and procedures on shoreline 
activities which include staff qualifications safety requirements, and staff-to-child 
ratios. 
B. 
Prior to participating in shoreline activities staff members must read and be 
instructed on the policies and procedures. 
C. 
The staff-to-child ratio while participating in shoreline activities must be at least 
one to ten (1:10). 
D. 
If children are permitted to wade in water that is more than twenty-four (24) 
inches deep, a certified lifeguard must be present and on duty. 
E. 
Before children are permitted to wade in water that is more than twenty-four (24) 
inches deep, swimming skills must be evaluated by properly trained swimming 
activity leaders. See rule section 2.606(A)(2). If determined by swimming staff, 
children must be wearing a United States Coast Guard approved personal 
flotation device sized appropriately to the activity and weight of the individual. 
2.608 WATERCRAFT ON FLATWATER 
If Children’s Resident Camps, School-Age Child Care Centers, or Neighborhood Youth 
Organizations offer watercraft on flatwater activities, the following regulations must be 
complied with: 
A. 
Qualifications:

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
309 
1. 
The watercraft instructor must meet one (1) of the following qualifications 
a 
Hold a current instructor certification from the American Canoe 
Association or another nationally recognized organization; 
b. 
Hold a current Red Cross lifeguard training certificate or equivalent 
training certificate from a nationally recognized organization; 
c. 
Hold a current American red cross basic water rescue certificate; or 
d. 
Eight (8) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge 
and skill in watercraft instruction and rescue skills specific to the 
watercraft activities to be conducted and have documented 
experience of engaging in the activity within the past two (2) years. 
2. 
Watercraft activity leaders must be at least eighteen (18) years of age and 
meet the following qualifications: 
a. 
Four (4) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge and 
skill in watercraft instruction specific to the watercraft activities to be 
conducted and have documented experience of engaging in the 
activity within the past two (2) years; and 
b. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by a 
Watercraft Instructor. 
3. 
Watercraft Staff must be at least sixteen (16) years of age and meet the 
following qualifications: 
a. 
Two (2) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge and 
skill specific to the watercraft activities taking place; and 
b. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by a 
Watercraft Instructor. 
B. 
Supervision 
1. 
Watercraft instructor or watercraft activity leader must be present for all 
watercraft activities. 
a. 
A watercraft instructor must be on site and available to all 
watercraft activity leaders while watercraft activities are taking 
place. 
2. 
A certified lifeguard must be present and on duty during all watercraft on 
flatwater activities; or

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
310 
a. 
A watercraft instructor with current Department-approved First Aid 
and CPR certification must be present and on duty during all 
watercraft on flatwater activities. 
3. 
The ratio while participating in watercraft on flatwater activities must be at 
least one to eight (1:8). 
4. 
There shall be a minimum of two (2) staff members at the shoreline and/or 
on the water at all times when children are on the water. Staff must be 
positioned in locations where they are able to provide effective 
surveillance, and in close enough proximity to respond to participants 
within thirty (30) seconds to respond and execute rescue in an incident or 
emergency. 
5. 
Before children are permitted to participate in watercraft activities, water 
safety skills must be evaluated by a watercraft instructor or properly 
trained watercraft activity leaders. 
6. 
There must be one (1) watercraft instructor, activity leader, or staff 
member in any watercraft other than a kayak or paddleboard with children 
under seven (7) years old. 
C. 
All staff and children on the water must be wearing a United States Coast Guard 
approved personal flotation device sized appropriate to the activity and weight of 
the individual. 
D. 
At no time shall the occupancy of the watercraft exceed the capacity established 
for the watercraft by the manufacturer. 
E. 
The watercraft must have on board a sound-producing device for signaling. Such 
a device may be operated by mouth, hand, or power and it must be able to be 
heard by persons on the water that indicates the need for participants and staff to 
return to the shore. 
F. 
Watercrafts shall not enter a swimming area when swimmers are in the water. 
2.609 WATERCRAFT ON CLASS I OR II MOVING WATER 
If Children’s Resident Camps, School-Age Child Care Centers, or Neighborhood Youth 
Organizations offer watercraft on class I or II moving water activities, the following 
regulations must be complied with: 
A. 
Qualifications: 
1. 
Watercraft Instructor on Class I or II moving water must meet the following 
qualifications:

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
311 
a. 
Must be familiar with rescue techniques with watercrafts on moving 
water, and meet one of the following qualifications: 
1. 
Hold a current Swiftwater rescue certification from a 
nationally recognized organization; or 
2. 
Hold a current American Red Cross basic water rescue 
certificate, hold a current Department-approved First Aid and 
CPR certification, and eight (8) hours of documented 
experience indicating knowledge and skill in watercraft 
instruction and rescue on class I or II moving water specific 
to the watercraft activities to be conducted and have 
documented experience of engaging in the activity within the 
past two (2) years; or 
3. 
Hold a current Red Cross lifeguard training certificate or 
equivalent training certificate from a nationally recognized 
organization and eight (8) hours of documented experience 
indicating knowledge and skill in watercraft instruction and 
rescue on class I or II moving water specific to the watercraft 
activities to be conducted and have documented experience 
of engaging in the activity within the past two (2) years. 
2. 
Watercraft activity leaders on class I or II moving water must be at least 
eighteen (18) years of age and meet the following qualifications: 
a. 
Four (4) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge and 
skill in in watercraft instruction and rescue on class I or II moving 
specific to the watercraft activities to be conducted and have 
documented experience of engaging in the activity within the past 
two (2) years; and 
b. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by a 
Watercraft Instructor on Class I or II moving water. 
3. 
Watercraft Staff must be at least sixteen (16) years of age and the 
following qualifications: 
a. 
Two (2) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge and 
skill specific to the watercraft activities taking place. 
b. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by a 
Watercraft Instructor on Class I or II moving water. 
B. 
Supervision 
1. 
A watercraft instructor on class I or II moving water must always present 
during all watercraft activities.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
312 
2. 
The ratio while participating in watercraft on class I or class II moving 
water activities must be at least one to eight (1:8). 
3. 
There must always be a minimum of two (2) staff members at the 
shoreline and/or on the water when children are on the water. Staff must 
be positioned in locations where they are able to provide effective 
surveillance, and in close enough proximity to respond to participants 
within thirty (30) seconds to execute rescue in an incident/emergency. 
a. 
Before children are permitted to participate in watercraft activities, 
water safety skills must be tested by properly trained watercraft 
staff members. 
b. 
There must be one watercraft instructor, activity leader or staff 
member in any watercraft other than a kayak or paddleboard with 
children under seven (7) years old. 
C. 
The watercraft instructor must train children and watercraft activity leaders and 
staff on rescue techniques on moving water. 
D. 
The program must have written policies and procedures on evaluating the safety 
of the river. Supervising staff must be trained on the policies and procedures. 
E. 
All staff and children on the water must be wearing a United States Coast Guard 
approved personal flotation device sized appropriate for the activity and to the 
weight of the individual. 
F. 
Float tubes are prohibited on class I or II moving water. 
2.610 WHITE WATER RAFTING ON CLASS III AND IV RIVERS (CLASSES OF 
RIVERS ARE THOSE AS DEFINED BY THE INTERNATIONAL SCALE OF 
RIVER DIFFICULTY) 
A. 
If the program operates white water rafting or kayaking, the program must have 
an active River Outfitter license as defined in section 33-32-102(6), C.R.S., from 
the Colorado Department of Natural Resources, Parks and Wildlife Commission. 
B. 
If a program provides a white-water rafting experience by purchase from a river 
outfitter, the license of the river outfitter must be active. 
ARCHERY, RIFLERY, AX-THROWING, AND USE OF KNIVES 
2.611 ARCHERY 
If Children’s Resident Camps, School-Age Child Care Centers, or Neighborhood Youth 
Organizations offer archery activities, the following regulations must be complied with: 
A. 
Qualifications

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
313 
1. 
Archery Instructor must meet one (1) of the following qualifications: 
a. 
Hold a current USA Archery Basic Archery Instructor level one (1) 
certification, a certification from a Nationally recognized 
organization; or 
b. 
Six (6) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge and 
skill in archery instruction specific to the archery activities taking 
place and have documented experience of engaging in the activity 
within the past two (2) years. 
2. 
Archery activity leaders must be at least eighteen (18) years of age must 
meet the following qualifications: 
a. 
Be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) from an archery 
instructor; 
b. 
Have three (3) hours of documented experience indicating 
knowledge and skill in archery specific to the archery activities 
taking place; and 
c. 
Have documented experience of engaging in the activity within the 
past two (2) years. 
3. 
Archery staff must be at least sixteen (16) years of age and meet the 
following qualifications: 
a. 
One and half (1.5) hours of documented experience indicating 
knowledge and skill in archery specific to the archery activities 
taking place; and 
b. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by an 
archery instructor. 
B. 
Supervision/ Ratios: 
1. 
An archery instructor or archery activity leader must be present at all times 
when children are present at the archery range or field. 
a. 
An archery instructor must be on site and available to all archery 
activity leaders while archery activities are taking place. 
2. 
For every eight (8) active archers there must be at least one (1) archery 
instructor or archery activity leader present. 
3. 
A qualified staff member must be present supervising observers and 
maintaining the ratios as defined at the specific ruleset the program is 
licensed as.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
314 
C. 
The archery range must be free from hazards and well-marked. There shall be a 
clear path to the target. Traffic, trail, or other camp activities must not be placed 
in the direction of the flight of the arrows. 
D. 
Equipment must be maintained in a safe condition. Bows and arrows must be 
inspected for fractures, splinters, or cracks before each use. Damaged bows and 
arrows must not be utilized. 
E. 
Equipment must be stored in a locked area when not in use. Bows and arrows 
shall be used only in the specified archery areas. 
F. 
All archers must use the same firing line. Arrows shall be issued only at the firing 
line by the archery instructor or archery activity leaders. 
G. 
Arrows shall be nocked to bow string after archers are on the firing line and after 
the signal to shoot has been given. 
H. 
Before arrows are released, archers shall have a definite target. 
I. 
Movement must be controlled by an archery instructor or archery activity leader. 
All participants must stay behind the firing line until the signal to retrieve arrows is 
given. All arrows shall be retrieved at the same time. 
K. 
Documentation of rules and procedures must be available for review at the 
archery range. 
L. 
If the program has field archery, written procedures must be posted to provide 
safety to the archers and include a procedure for check-in and out of archers and 
all equipment. 
M. 
Archery tag is prohibited. 
2.612 RIFLERY 
If Children’s Resident Camps, School-Age Child Care Centers, or Neighborhood Youth 
Organizations offer riflery activities, the following regulations must be complied with: 
A. 
Qualifications 
1. 
Range instructor must be at least twenty-one (21) years of age and must 
meet one (1) of the following qualifications: 
a. 
Hold a current National Rifle Association instructor's certification; or 
b. 
Sixteen (16) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge 
and skill in riflery instruction specific to the riflery activities taking 
place and have documented experience of engaging in the activity 
within the past two (2) years.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
315 
2. 
Range activity leader must be at least eighteen (18) years of age and 
must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by a riflery 
instructor and meet one (1) of the following qualifications: 
a. 
Hold a current National Rifle Association (NRA) Range Safety 
Officer certification; 
b. 
Have documentation of a current Hunter Safety Instructor 
Certification; or 
c. 
Eight (8) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge 
and skill in riflery specific to the riflery activities taking place and 
have documented experience of engaging in the activity within the 
past two (2) years. 
3. 
Range staff must be at least eighteen (18) years of age and meet the 
following qualifications: 
a. 
Four (4) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge and 
skill in riflery specific to the riflery activities taking; and 
b. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by a riflery 
instructor. 
B. 
Supervision: 
1. 
For every six (6) active participants there must be one (1) range instructor 
or range activity leader present. 
2. 
The following individuals must always be present at the firing line while 
participants are present: 
a. 
A range instructor is to directly supervise all live fire on the range. 
(1) 
If more than one (1) range is active a range instructor must 
be on site and available to all range activity leaders while 
rifle activities are taking place. 
C. 
The rifle range must be free from all hazards, away from other activities and 
traffic of any type; be well marked with danger signs or flags; and all blind 
approaches must be fenced or blocked off. 
1. 
The range must have a clearly visible sign, or range warning flag system, 
indicating the operating status of the range (e.g. “CAUTION RANGE IN 
USE”/ “RANGE CLOSED”)”. 
D. 
Firearms and ammunition must be locked and stored separately.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
316 
E. 
The range must be constructed with an appropriately designed bullet-stop so that 
all bullets will be stopped behind the targets. The bullet-stop must be free of 
trees, rocks, boulders, or other objects which may cause a bullet to ricochet from 
or overshoot the bullet-stop. 
F. 
There must be a well-defined firing line with firing points/ lanes that assist 
participants in locating their correct target, ensure participants do not interfere 
with each other during firing; and allow the range instructor or range activity 
leader to supervise shooters, clear firearm malfunctions, or to otherwise assist 
shooters as needed. 
1. 
The firing line surface must provide shooters with firm footing. If the firing 
line is elevated, it must be constructed to provide safe movement of 
participants on and off the elevated area. 
G. 
Targets must be placed as close to the backstop as practical to elevate off the 
ground to prevent bullet ricochet off the range floor. Targets shall be constructed 
of paper, cardboard, wood, or plastic. Steel or glass targets are not permitted. 
1. 
Target holders must be constructed of low ricochet materials such as 
wood or plastic. 
H. 
Only the following types of guns shall be permitted: 
1. 
.22 caliber rimfire, single-shot, bolt-action rifles having no trigger 
modification other than the factory setting. 
2. 
Pneumatic spring-type and CO2 air guns may be either .22 caliber or .177 
(Ball Bearing (BB) size). 
I. 
All participants must always wear protective eye equipment. 
J. 
All participants must wear appropriate hearing protection when using .22 caliber 
rimfire, single-shot, bolt-action rifles. All observers and anyone within the range 
area must wear appropriate hearing protection when .22 caliber rimfire, single-
shot, bolt-action rifles are in use. 
K. 
The range instructor or the range activity leader must maintain or supervise the 
proper condition of the firearms, inspect firearms before and after usage, and 
clean firearms, as necessary. Firearms that do not function properly must be 
repaired and tested before usage. 
L. 
Instruction on the use of firearms must be reviewed with all participants prior to 
participating in the activity. 
M. 
Range rules and emergency procedures must be posted at the range.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
317 
N. 
The range instructor or range activity leader must distribute cartridges at the 
firing line only. No more than five (5) cartridges at a time should be distributed to 
a participant. 
O. 
Firing must only be permitted at the firing line. 
1. 
Observers must remain a minimum of fifteen (15) feet behind the firing line 
at all times. If not firing or training, observers must not be in the firing line 
area. 
P. 
Any firearm that is not on the firing line ready to fire must have the magazine or 
cartridge feeding device removed and the chamber unloaded with the action 
open. 
Q. 
All firearms must be unloaded immediately upon the command “cease firing” 
regardless of when this command is given. Firearm actions must remain open 
until further commands are given. 
R. 
Prior to anyone going downrange, or towards the target area, all firearms must 
have the magazine or cartridge feeding device removed, the chamber unloaded 
with the action open, the muzzle of the firearm pointed at a safe direction, and 
movement must be controlled by the range instructor and the range activity 
leader. A range instructor or range activity leader must remain at the firing line 
with all firearms. 
S. 
All spent or unspent cartridges must be returned to the range instructor or range 
activity leader. 
2.613 AX-THROWING 
If Children’s Resident Camps, School-Age Child Care Centers, or Neighborhood Youth 
Organizations offer Ax-throwing activities, the following regulations must be complied 
with: 
A. 
Qualifications 
1. 
The ax-throwing instructor must meet the following qualifications: 
a. 
Six (6) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge and 
skill training or in ax-throwing instruction specific to the ax-throwing 
activities taking place and have documented experience of 
engaging in the activity within the past two (2) years. 
2. 
Ax-throwing activity leaders must be at least eighteen (18) years of age 
and meet the following:

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
318 
a. 
Three (3) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge 
and skill in ax- throwing specific to the ax-throwing activities taking 
place and have documented experience of engaging in the activity 
within the past two (2) years; and 
b. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by an ax-
throwing instructor. 
3. 
Ax-throwing staff must be at least sixteen (16) years of age and meet the 
following: 
a. 
One and half (1.5) hours of documented experience indicating 
knowledge and skill in ax-throwing specific to the ax-throwing 
activities taking place; and 
b. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by an ax-
throwing instructor. 
B. 
Supervision/ Ratios: 
1. 
An ax-throwing instructor or ax-throwing activity leader must be present at 
all times when children are present at the Ax-Throwing range. 
a. 
An ax-throwing instructor must be on site and available to all ax-
throwing activity leaders while ax-throwing activities are taking 
place. 
2. 
For every eight (8) throwers there must be at least one ax-throwing 
instructor or one ax-throwing activity leader present. 
C. 
The ax-throwing course must be free from hazards and well-marked. There shall 
be a clear, unobstructed path to the target. Traffic, trail, or other camp activities 
must not be placed in the direction of the path of the axes. 
D. 
The ax-throwing course must have a waiting line and a throwing line that are at 
least five (5) feet from each other. 
E. 
Equipment must be maintained in a safe condition. Prior to each use axes must 
be inspected for fractures, splinters, or cracks in the handle. The head of the ax 
must be secure to the handle with no movement. Damaged axes must not be 
utilized. 
F. 
Equipment must be stored in a locked area when not in use. Axes shall be used 
only in the specified ax-throwing areas. 
G. 
All ax throwers shall use the same throwing line. Axes shall be issued only at the 
throwing line.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
319 
H. 
Axes shall not be thrown until after the signal to throw has been given. 
I. 
Before an ax is released, throwers must have a definite target. Targets must be 
appropriate for ax throwing. 
J. 
Movement must be controlled by an ax-throwing instructor or ax-throwing activity 
leader. All persons must stay behind the throwing line until the signal to retrieve 
axes is given. All axes shall be retrieved at the same time and placed in a 
designated area. 
K. 
Ax-throwing participants must wear closed-toed shoes. Instructors or activity 
leaders will need to check participants for any clothing that could obstruct a 
participant’s throwing movement or vision including but not limited to scarves, 
hoods, or loose-fitting clothing. 
L. 
Instruction on the use of axes, proper throwing techniques must be reviewed with 
all participants prior to participating in the activity. 
M. 
The ax must never be thrown backwards or from the side. 
N. 
Documentation of rules and procedures must be available for review. 
2.614 USE OF KNIFES 
If Children’s Resident Camps, School-Age Child Care Centers, or Neighborhood Youth 
Organizations offer knife use activities, the following regulations must be complied with: 
A. 
Qualifications 
1. 
All staff participating must be trained in the usage of knives and in the 
facilities, policies and procedures and have a current Department-
approved first aid and CPR training certification. 
2.  
All staff participating must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) 
from a supervisor. 
B. 
Supervision 
1. 
Program must develop supervision plans and supervision must be 
appropriate to the activities and ages of participants. Plans must be 
available for review by the Department. 
C. 
The program must have policies and procedures regarding the developmentally 
appropriate practice for the use of knives. The policies and procedures must 
include the following; 
1. 
Knife safety; 
2. 
Size of blades;

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
320 
3. 
Types of knives used; 
4. 
Appropriate supervision and staff to child ratios while using knives; and 
5. 
Storage of knives. 
D. 
Knife usage policies and emergency procedures must be reviewed with all 
participants prior to participating in the activity. 
1. 
Documentation of rules and procedures must be available for review. 
HORSEBACK RIDING 
2.615 HORSEBACK RIDING ACTIVITIES 
If Children’s Resident Camps, School-Age Child Care Centers, or Neighborhood Youth 
Organizations offer horseback riding activities the following rules must be complied with: 
A. 
Qualifications: 
1. 
The horseback riding Instructor must meet one (1) of the following 
qualifications: 
a. 
A current certificate from a nationally recognized organization or 
riding school; or 
b. 
Twenty (20) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge 
and skill in horseback riding instruction specific to the horseback 
riding activities taking place and have documented experience of 
engaging in the activity within the past two (2) years. 
2. 
Horseback riding activity leader must be at least eighteen (18) years of 
age and meet the following qualifications: 
a. 
Ten (10) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge 
and skill in horseback riding instruction specific to the horseback 
riding activities taking place and have documented experience of 
engaging in the activity within the past two (2) years; and 
b. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by a 
horseback riding instructor. 
3. 
Horseback riding staff must be at least sixteen (16) years of age and meet 
the following qualifications: 
a. 
Five (5) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge and 
skill in horseback riding specific to the horseback riding activities 
taking place; and

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
321 
b. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by a 
horseback riding instructor. 
B. 
Supervision 
1. 
There must be one (1) horseback riding instructor or horseback riding 
activity leader present for every ten (10) or fewer children participating in 
the riding program. 
a. 
A horseback riding instructor must be on site and available to all 
horseback riding activity leaders and staff. 
2. 
Trail Ride: 
a. 
There must be an individual with current Department-approved 
CPR and First Aid certification present for each trail ride. 
b. 
There must be at least two (2) staff present for each trail ride 
meeting the following qualifications: 
1. 
A riding instructor or riding activity leader; and 
2. 
A riding staff member. 
c. 
Staff must have a communications plan during all trail rides. 
C. 
No participant is allowed in the barn area and riding area unless the horseback 
riding instructor or a Riding activity leader is present. 
D. 
The riding instructor or riding activity leader must determine the child's riding 
experience and level of skill and must take these into account in assigning which 
horse each child should ride and determining the type of riding activity in which 
each child should engage. 
E. 
The emergency procedures must be posted in the barn, stable, ring, or 
commonly used areas and include information required in section 13-21-119, 
C.R.S. 
F. 
The riding supervisor or riding instructor must review all riding rules with 
participants prior to participating in any riding activities. 
G. 
Children and staff shall be appropriately dressed for riding, which must include 
closed toed shoes or boots and long pants. 
H. 
The riding supervisor or riding instructor must evaluate the footgear of each child 
and make the stirrups safe for each child's shoe or boot.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
322 
I. 
All children and staff must wear properly fitted helmets designed for equestrian 
use according to ASTM F1163-15 standards while riding as defined and 
explained by ASTM international at https://www.play.org/f1163-15.html (February 
2023), herein incorporated by reference. No later editions or amendments are 
incorporated. These resources are available at no cost from ASTM International 
at ASTM.org. These resources are also available for public inspection and 
copying at the Colorado Department of Early Childhood, 710 S. Ash St., Denver, 
CO 80246, during regular business hours. 
1. 
Helmets must be replaced according to the manufacturer's 
recommendations or at least every five (5) years. 
J. 
The horseback riding equipment shall be in good condition, properly sized and 
adjusted for each rider. All equipment must be used and maintained according to 
the manufacture recommendations. 
K. 
Any hazardous items and materials including but not limited to tools and 
medications must be inaccessible to children. 
L. 
The horse barn or stable, ring, and commonly used trail(s) shall be in good repair 
and free of dangerous obstructions. 
M. 
Horses shall be cared for with evidence of an adequate feeding schedule, fresh 
water must be readily available and procedures in place to care for sick horses. 
N. 
Horses must not be permitted in the other designated activity areas. 
CLIMBING 
2.616 ROCK CLIMBING AND CLIMBING WALLS 
If Children’s Resident Camps, School-Age Child Care Centers, or Neighborhood Youth 
Organizations offer basic/top roped climbing, which includes such topics as the care 
and use of basic equipment, knots, and belaying, verbal signals, and or techniques of 
rappelling, the following rules must be complied with: 
A. 
Qualifications: 
1. 
Climbing instructor must meet one (1) of the following qualifications: 
a. 
Have a current top-roped climbing instructor certification; or 
b. 
Sixteen (16) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge 
and skill in knots, anchors, safety zones, verbal signals, belaying, 
rappelling, and safe tie-ins, and climbing instruction specific to the 
rock-climbing activities taking place, and have documented 
experience of engaging in the activity within the past two (2) years.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
323 
c. 
If an auto-belay device is used: 
(1) 
The instructor must have four (4) hours of documented 
experience indicating knowledge and skill in use and 
operation of the auto belay device, knots, safety zones, 
verbal signals, belaying, rappelling, and safe tie-ins, specific 
to the climbing activities taking place, and have documented 
experience of engaging in the activity within the past two (2) 
years. 
2. 
Climbing activity leaders must be at least (18) years of age, have 
documentation of a skills verification, must be trained as outlined in rule 
section 2.605(F)(1) by a climbing instructor and meet one (1) of the 
following qualifications: 
a. 
Must have verified knowledge of technical climbing by completion 
of a course or climbing school; or 
b. 
Eight (8) hours of documented experience from a climbing 
supervisor indicating knowledge and skill in knots, safety zones, 
verbal signals, belaying, rappelling, and safe tie-ins, and climbing 
instruction specific to the rock-climbing activities taking place and 
have documented experience of engaging in the activity within the 
past two (2) years. 
c. 
If an auto-belay device is used: 
(1) 
The activity leader must have at least two (2) hours of 
documented experience indicating knowledge and skill in 
use and operation of the auto belay device, knots, safety 
zones, verbal signals, belaying, rappelling, and safe tie-ins, 
specific to the climbing activities taking place, and have 
documented experience of engaging in the activity within the 
past two (2) years. 
3. 
Climbing staff must be at least sixteen (16) years of age and meet the 
following qualifications: 
a.  
Four (4) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge and 
skill in knots, anchors, safety zones, verbal signals, belaying, 
rappelling, and safe tie-ins, specific to the rock-climbing activities 
taking place, and have documented experience of engaging in the 
activity within the past two (2) years. 
b. 
If an auto-belay device is used:

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
324 
(1) 
The climbing staff must have at least one (1) hour of 
documented experience indicating knowledge and skill in 
use and operation of the auto belay device, knots, safety 
zones, verbal signals, belaying, rappelling, and safe tie-ins, 
specific to the climbing activities taking place, and have 
documented experience of engaging in the activity within the 
past two (2) years. 
B. 
Supervision: 
1. 
At least two (2) rock-climbing staff must be present at the climbing site at 
all times. At least one of the staff must be a rock-climbing instructor or 
activity leader. 
a. 
A rock-climbing instructor must be on site and available to all rock-
climbing activity leaders and climbing staff while rock climbing 
activities are taking place. 
2. 
For every eight (8) active climbers there must be at least one (1) rock 
climbing instructor or rock-climbing activity leader present. 
3. 
A qualified staff member must be present supervising observers 
maintaining the ratios as defined at the specific ruleset the program is 
licensed as. 
C. 
The climbing instructor shall approve guidelines for the proper maintenance of all 
climbing equipment used. Equipment shall be checked by the instructor or 
activity leader immediately prior to use. 
D. 
All rock-climbing equipment shall be maintained and replaced according to the 
manufacture recommendations and be visually and physically inspected before 
each climb. 
E. 
Climbers in a natural outdoor environment must wear helmets specifically 
designed for the activity at all times when in designated helmet zones. 
1. 
When an auto belay device is used, a helmet should not be worn. 
F. 
The program shall not permit an unsupervised climb. 
G. 
The climbing supervisor or climbing activity leader must have knowledge of 
where the climb will occur and must give approval prior to the activity taking 
place. 
H. 
Each rock climber must be visually supervised.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
325 
I. 
All climbers and rappellers shall be belayed in a manner consistent with current 
industry standards. 
J. 
Belayers must be instructed in proper procedures, and directly supervised until 
their skills have been verified by a climbing instructor. 
2.617 SINGLE AND/OR MULTI-PITCH CLIMBING (DOES NOT INCLUDE TOP-
ROPED CLIMBING) 
If Children’s Resident Camps, School-Age Child Care Centers, or Neighborhood Youth 
Organizations offer single or multi-pitch climbing, the following rules must be complied 
with: 
A. 
Qualifications: 
1. 
Single or multi-pitch climbing instructors must meet the one (1) of following 
qualifications: 
a. 
An American Mountain Guides Association (AMGA) multi-pitch 
instructor course and have passed the AMGA Single Pitch 
Instructor assessment; or 
b. 
Sixteen (16) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge 
and skill in knots, anchors, safety zones, verbal signals, belaying, 
rappelling, and safe tie-ins, and climbing instruction specific to the 
rock-climbing activities taking place; and 
(1) 
Documentation that the individual has led or shared lead on 
ten (10) single or multi-pitch rock routes within the last two 
(2) years. 
2. 
Single or multi- pitch climbing activity leaders must be at least eighteen 
(18) years of age and have knowledge of rescue techniques, 
documentation of a skills verification, must be trained as outlined in rule 
section 2.605(F)(1) by a climbing instructor and meet one (1) of the 
following qualifications: 
a. 
Have a current AMGA single pitch instructor certification; or 
b. 
Eight (8) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge 
and skill in knots, anchors, safety zones, verbal signals, belaying, 
rappelling, and safe tie-ins, and climbing instruction specific to the 
rock-climbing activities taking place and have documented 
experience of engaging in the activity within the past two (2) years. 
3. 
Climbing staff must be at least sixteen (16) years of age and meet the 
following qualifications:

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
326 
a. 
Four (4) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge and 
skill in knots, anchors, safety zones, verbal signals, belaying, 
rappelling, and safe tie-ins, specific to the rock-climbing activities 
taking place, and have documented experience of engaging in the 
activity within the past two (2) years; and 
b. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by a single or 
multipitch climbing instructor. 
B. 
Supervision: 
1. 
At least two (2) staff must be present at the climbing site at all times one of 
the two (2) staff must be a single or multi pitch climbing instructor or 
activity leader. 
a. 
A single or multi pitch rock-climbing instructor must be on site and 
available to all rock-climbing activity leaders while rock climbing 
activities are taking place. 
2. 
For every three (3) climbers there must be at least one rock climbing 
instructor or rock-climbing activity leader present. 
C. 
No climbing instructor shall take participants on a climb the climbing instructor 
has not completed previously. 
D. 
The multi-pitch climbing instructor must assess the ability of all children 
participating as to the difficulty of the climb. 
E. 
The single or multi-pitch climbing instructor must have knowledge of where the 
climb will occur and must give approval prior to the activity taking place. 
F. 
No child will be the rope leader unless their skills have been verified by a 
climbing instructor. 
2.618 HIGH AND/OR LOW ROPES CHALLENGE COURSES AND ZIPLINES 
If Children’s Resident Camps, School-Age Child Care Centers, or Neighborhood Youth 
Organizations offer high and/or low ropes challenge courses, a climbing wall as part of a 
ropes course, or ziplines the following rules must be complied with: 
A. 
Qualifications: 
1. 
Challenge course instructor must meet one (1) of the following 
qualifications:

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
327 
a. 
Hold a current certification specific to that activity or challenge 
course “system” from a recognized organization or certifying body. 
If the certificate does not have an “expiration date,” the certificate 
must have been completed within the past two (2) years; and the 
supervisor must have documented experience of engaging in the 
activity within the past two (2) years; 
b. 
If the course involves high ropes the challenge course instructor 
must have sixteen (16) hours of documented experience indicating 
knowledge and skill in challenge course instruction related to the 
challenge course activities taking place and have documented 
experience of engaging in the activity within the past two (2) years; 
or 
c. 
If the course involves only low ropes the challenge course instructor 
must have eight (8) hours documented experience indicating 
knowledge and skill in challenge course instruction related to the 
challenge course activities taking place and have documented 
experience of engaging in the activity within the past two (2) years. 
2. 
The challenge course activity leader must be at least eighteen (18) years 
of age, must have documentation of skills verification, and must be trained 
as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) from an individual that is qualified as 
a challenge course instructor and must meet the following qualifications: 
a. 
If the course involves high ropes the challenge course activity 
leader must have ten (10) hours of documented experience 
indicating knowledge and skill in challenge course instruction 
specific to the challenge course activities taking place, and have 
documented experience of engaging in the activity within the past 
two (2) years; and 
b. 
If the course involves only low ropes the challenge course activity 
leader must have five (5) hours of documented experience 
indicating knowledge and skill in challenge course instruction to the 
challenge course activities taking place and have documented 
experience of engaging in the activity within the past two (2) years. 
3. 
Challenge course staff must be at least sixteen (16) years of age and must 
be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) from an individual that is 
qualified as a challenge course instructor and meet one (1) of the following 
qualifications: 
a. 
If the course involves high ropes the challenge course staff must 
have five (5) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge 
and skill in challenge course instruction specific to the challenge 
course activities taking place; or

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
328 
b. 
If the course involves only low ropes, the challenge course staff 
must have three (3) hours of documented experience indicating 
knowledge and skill in challenge course instruction specific to the 
challenge course activities taking place. 
B. 
Supervision: 
1. 
At least two (2) staff must be present at the course site at all times. One 
(1) of the two (2) staff members must be a challenge course activity 
leader. 
a. 
A challenge course instructor must be on site and available to all 
challenge course activity leaders while challenge course activities 
are taking place. 
b. 
For every eight (8) participants there must be at least one challenge 
course instructor or challenge course activity leader present. 
C. 
Ropes course elements must have written evidence of annual inspection for 
integrity of all hardware, materials, and equipment by an individual qualified 
through a nationally recognized organization such as: Association of Challenge 
Course Technology (ACCT). 
D. 
Ropes courses must be use as designed and inspected regularly by the rope 
supervisor or the rope instructor. 
E. 
All equipment and elements of a rope course must be safety checked prior to 
each use and have written records of regular inspection and maintenance of all 
equipment and elements utilized. Equipment must be maintained and replaced 
per manufactures’ recommendations. 
F. 
Children must wear safety equipment appropriate for the activity. 
G. 
Children must wear properly fitted helmets when using the high ropes course. 
H. 
At all times, there must be a rope supervisor or rope instructor on the ropes 
course with children. 
I. 
Ropes courses must be off limits to children when a rope supervisor or rope 
instructor is not present and access to ropes course must be controlled 
J. 
The program must have written safety procedures for use of the ropes course(s). 
Staff must be trained in the safety procedures. 
HIKING, BACKPACKING, AND CAMPING 
2.619 HIKING

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
329 
If School-Age Child Care Centers, Children’s Resident Camps, or Neighborhood Youth 
Organizations offer hiking activities, the following rules must be complied with: 
A. 
Qualifications 
1. 
Hiking instructor must meet the following qualifications: 
a. 
Hold a current Department-approved First Aid certification; and 
b. 
Six (6) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge and 
skill in the symptoms and correct treatment procedures for 
hypothermia and dehydration and hiking instruction specific to the 
hiking activities taking place and have documented experience of 
engaging in the activity within the past two (2) years. 
2. 
Hiking activity leaders must be at least eighteen (18) years of age and 
meet the following qualifications: 
a. 
Three (3) hours of experience specific to the hiking activities taking 
place; 
b. 
Hold a current Department-approved First Aid certification; and 
c. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by a hiking 
instructor. 
3. 
Hiking staff must be at least sixteen (16) years of age and meet the 
following qualifications: 
a. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by a hiking 
instructor; and 
b. 
One and a half (1.5) hours of documented experience indicating 
knowledge and skill in hiking specific to the hiking activities taking 
place. 
B. 
Supervision & Ratios 
1. 
Staff must continually observe and monitor participants on the trail 
including monitoring of symptoms including but not limited to sunburn, 
dehydration, fatigue, hypothermia, and heat related illness. 
2. 
At least two (2) hiking activity leaders must accompany a group in hikes. 
Hiking groups may divide up as long as hikers are always with one activity 
leader and activity leaders are in visual, verbal or electronic (radio or 
wireless communication) contact with each other.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
330 
C. 
In selecting the area for hiking, the hiking instructor must consider the hiker’s 
age, physical condition, and experience, as well as the season, weather trends 
during the trip, methods of evacuation, and communication. 
D. 
The program must have written safety procedures for hiking, including the written 
policies and procedures for evacuating a child that becomes sick or injured on a 
hike. Hiking activity leaders and children must be trained on the safety 
procedures and policies. 
E. 
Before participation, children must be instructed on: 
1. 
The fundamental safety procedures to follow on the trail; 
2. 
Procedures to follow if separated from the group; 
3. 
Proper health and sanitation procedures on the trail; 
4. 
Rules and regulations of the governing land where the hiking occurs; 
5. 
Potential high-risk areas; 
6. 
Environmental hazard; and 
7. 
Procedures when encountering animals. 
F. 
Each hiker shall be equipped with protective clothing against natural elements 
such as rain, snow, wind, cold, sun, and insects. 
G. 
An itinerary of the hiking trip and a list of all participants on the hike must be kept 
at the program. 
H. 
If any off-trail hiking occurs during the trip, staff must have experience in traveling 
off trail including back country navigation. 
2.620 BACKPACKING AND CAMPING 
If Children’s Resident Camps, School-Age Child Care Centers, or Neighborhood Youth 
Organizations offer backpacking or camping trips where the basic needs for operation, 
such as places of dwelling, water supply systems, and permanent toilet and or cooking 
facilities are not usually provided, the overnight requirements for each type of program 
must be followed according to rules for that license type in addition to the following 
requirements: 
A. 
Qualifications 
1. 
Backpacking/camping instructor must meet the following qualifications: 
a. 
Hold a current Department-approved First Aid and CPR 
certification; and

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
331 
b. 
Eight (8) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge 
and skill in the symptoms and correct treatment procedures for 
hypothermia and dehydration and backpacking and camping 
instruction specific to the backpacking and camping activities taking 
place and have documented experience of engaging in the activity 
within the past two (2) years. 
2. 
Backpacking/Camping activity leaders must be at least eighteen (18) 
years of age and meet the following qualifications: 
a. 
Hold a current Department-approved First Aid certification; 
b. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by a 
backpacking/ camping instructor; and 
c. 
Four (4) hours of experience specific to the backpacking/camping 
activities taking place. 
3. 
Backpacking/Camping staff must be at least sixteen (16) years of age and 
meet the following qualifications: 
a. 
Two (2) hours of experience specific to the backpacking/camping 
activities taking place; and 
b. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by a 
backpacking/ camping instructor. 
B. 
Supervision and Ratios 
1. 
Staff must continually observe and monitor participants on the trip 
including monitoring of symptoms including but not limited to: sunburn, 
dehydration, fatigue, hypothermia, and heat related illness. 
2. 
Appropriate staff-to-child ratios must be maintained, but there must be at 
least two (2) staff members accompanying each trip. One (1) staff member 
must be at least eighteen (18) years of age, unless otherwise defined in 
an applicable rule. 
a. 
If the program license type allows the trip to exceed two (2) nights, 
there must be one (1) backpacking/camping instructor who is at 
least twenty-one (21) years of age. 
3. 
At no time may a child be left without qualified supervision. Sleeping 
quarters of the staff must be within sight or hearing distance of the 
sleeping quarters of the children whom they supervise.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
332 
4. 
Children must sleep in the same room or tent with individuals who are 
consistent with their gender identity. This rule is intended to mirror the 
requirements of the Colorado Anti-Discrimination Act (CADA), for places 
of public accommodation, sections 24-34-600.3 through 24-34-605, 
C.R.S., and its implementing regulations at 3 CCR 708-1. Rule 81.9 
(December 30, 2023), as incorporated by reference in rule section 
2.235(D)(1). The Department does not provide advisory opinions about 
whether an entity is covered by CADA. 
5. 
In gender-segregated facilities where undressing in the presence of others 
occurs, camps shall make reasonable accommodations to allow access 
consistent with an individual's gender identity. This rule is intended to 
mirror the requirements of the Colorado Anti-Discrimination Act (CADA), 
for places of public accommodation, sections 24-34-600.3 through 24-34-
605, C.R.S., and its implementing regulations at 3 CCR 708-1. Rule 81.9 
(December 30, 2023), as incorporated by reference in rule section 
2.235(D)(1). The Department does not provide advisory opinions about 
whether an entity is covered by CADA. 
C. 
The backpacking /camping instructor shall consider the hiker's age, physical 
condition, and experience, as well as the season, weather trends during the trip, 
methods of evacuation and communication, and availability of water when 
selecting the area for backpacking or camping. 
D. 
The program must have written safety procedures for backpacking or camping, 
including the written policies and procedures for evacuating a child that becomes 
sick or injured. Staff and children must be trained in the safety policies and 
procedures. 
E. 
Before participation, children shall have a safety orientation and be instructed on 
the applicable precautions, such as: 
1. 
The fundamental safety procedures to follow on the trip; 
2. 
Procedures for a hiker if separated from the group; 
3. 
Proper health procedures, including the need for drinking fluids and eating 
appropriate foods; 
4. 
Sanitation procedures; 
5. 
Rules and regulations of the governing land where the camping or 
backpacking occurs; 
6. 
Potential high-risk areas which may be found on the trip; 
7. 
Environmental hazards; and

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
333 
8. 
Procedures when encountering animals. 
F. 
Children shall be oriented to minimum impact guidelines and techniques. 
G. 
Each child shall be equipped with protective clothing and equipment against 
anticipated natural elements such as rain, snow, wind, cold, sun, and insects. 
H. 
Adequate shelters such as a tent must be available for each child. The shelter 
occupancy must be in compliance with the manufacturers’ recommendations. 
1. 
All structures used by children must be kept in good repair at all times. 
2. 
If fabric structures are used, they must be constructed of fire and flame-
retardant material. 
I. 
Each child must be provided with their own mat, pad, bed, sleeping bag, or cot. 
J. 
The program must have emergency plans for all locations. 
1. 
Plans must be available for the Department to review. 
2. 
Plans must be available for parents or guardians. 
3. 
All staff must be trained in emergency plans for all trip locations prior to 
trips. 
K. 
There must be a day-to-day itinerary prepared prior to departure. 
1. 
The Itinerary must include a list of all participants. 
2. 
Sources of emergency care and methods of communication with such 
facilities as hospitals, police, and forest service must be identified for each 
campsite on the itinerary. 
3. 
The program director must have access to a copy of the itinerary. 
4. 
The itinerary must be followed as closely as possible. 
5. 
The program director must be notified of an itinerary change as soon as 
possible. 
6. 
The itinerary must be available to the Department, parents, and local 
police.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
334 
L. 
Programs must have a contingency plan/plan for facilities to use during adverse 
weather and air quality index advisory Unhealthy for Sensitive Groups explained 
by the Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) at 
https://www.airnow.gov/sites/default/files/2018-04/aqi_brochure_02_14_0.pdf 
(Feb. 2024), herein incorporated by reference. No later editions or amendments 
are incorporated. These resources are available at no cost from the 
Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) at https://www.airnow.gov/aqi/aqi-
basics/. These resources are also available for public inspection and copying at 
the Colorado Department of Early Childhood, 710 S. Ash St., Denver, CO 80246, 
during regular business hours. The plan must be available to parents/guardians. 
M. 
A copy of the current statement which has been signed and dated by the parent 
or guardian indicating that the camp staff may obtain emergency medical care 
must be readily available to the staff accompanying the participants. 
N. 
If any off-trail backpacking or camping occurs during the trip, staff must have 
experience in traveling off trail including back country navigation. 
BIKING 
2.621 BIKING ON PUBLIC ROADS OR MOUNTAIN TRAILS 
If Children’s Resident Camps, School-Age Child Care Centers, or Neighborhood Youth 
Organizations offer bicycling trips, the following rules must be complied with: 
A. 
Staff Qualifications 
1. 
The biking instructor must meet the following qualifications: 
a. 
Hold a current Department-approved First Aid certification; and 
b. 
Six (6) hours of documented experience indicating knowledge and 
skill in biking specific to the biking activities taking place, and must 
be familiar with state laws about bicycling; be knowledgeable about 
the type of bicycling terrain where the bicycle trips will occur; know 
how to make simple bicycle repairs; how to properly fit a bike and 
select necessary equipment; and have documented experience of 
engaging in the activity within the past two (2) years. 
2. 
Biking activity leaders must be at least eighteen (18) years of age and 
meet the following qualifications: 
a. 
Hold a current Department-approved First Aid certification; and 
b. 
Biking activity leaders must be trained as outlined in rule section 
2.605(F)(1) by a biking instructor; and

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
335 
c. 
Three (3) hours of experience specific to the biking activities taking 
place. 
3. 
Biking Staff must be at least sixteen (16) years of age and meet the 
following qualifications: 
a. 
Must be trained as outlined in rule section 2.605(F)(1) by a biking 
instructor; and 
b. 
One and a half (1.5) hours of experience specific to the biking 
activities taking place. 
B. 
Supervision and Ratios 
1. 
For every eight (8) bikers there must be at least one (1) biking instructor or 
biking activity leader present. 
2. 
At least two (2) biking staff must accompany a group while biking. One (1) 
must be a biking activity leader. 
3. 
Biking groups may divide up as long as bikers are always with one (1) 
activity leader and activity leaders are in visual, verbal or electronic (radio 
or wireless communication) contact with each other. 
C. 
The program must have written safety procedures of bike trips, including the 
written policies for evacuating a child that becomes sick or injured on a bike trip. 
Staff and children must be trained on the safety procedures and policies. 
D. 
Each rider shall wear head protection specifically designed for the type of biking 
activity according to ASTM F1447-18 standards while riding as defined and 
explained by ASTM international at https://www.astm.org/f1447-18.html (June 25, 
2018), herein incorporated by reference. No later editions or amendments are 
incorporated. These resources are available at no cost from ASTM International 
at ASTM.org. These resources are also available for public inspection and 
copying at the Colorado Department of Early Childhood, 710 S. Ash St., Denver, 
CO 80246, during regular business hours. 
E. 
The bicycle shall be equipped with brakes in working condition. Bicycles must be 
properly maintained, inspected prior to each bicycling trip, and adjusted to the 
size of the child riding the bicycle. 
F. 
Equipment must be maintained and replaced per manufacturers’ 
recommendations. 
G. 
If the program allows children to use their own bicycles the biking staff or 
supervisor must inspect the bike to verify that the bicycle is appropriate for the 
activity, in good condition, properly maintained, and adjusted to the size of the 
child riding the bicycle prior to participating.

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
336 
H. 
An appropriate bicycle repair kit must be taken on each trip. 
I. 
The biking supervisor or staff must instruct children as to emergency procedures, 
safe riding practices, and road and trail etiquette. 
J. 
The biking supervisor or staff shall evaluate each child as to their physical 
capability to participate in the planned bicycling trip, keeping in mind the trip 
length, terrain, altitude of the trip, and weather conditions. 
K. 
An itinerary of the biking trip and a list of all participants on the biking trip must be 
kept at the program. 
2.700 RULES REGULATING NEIGHBORHOOD YOUTH ORGANIZATIONS 
2.701 AUTHORITY 
These rules and regulations are adopted pursuant to the rulemaking authority provided 
in section 26.5-1-105(1), C.R.S., and are intended to be consistent with the 
requirements of the State Administrative Procedure Act, section 24-4-101, C.R.S., et 
seq. (the “APA”), the Anna Jo Garcia Haynes Early Childhood Act, section 26.5-1-101, 
C.R.S., et seq. (the “Early Childhood Act”), and the Child Care Licensing Act, section 
26.5-5-301, C.R.S., et seq. 
The specific rulemaking authorities granted for Neighborhood Youth Organizations 
include section 26.5-5-308(2), C.R.S. 
2.702 SCOPE AND PURPOSE 
The Colorado Department of Early Childhood, Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and 
Administration is responsible for the administration of health and safety rules and 
requirements for licensed child care facilities. These rules outline the requirements for 
Neighborhood Youth Organizations. These rules shall govern the health and safety 
requirements for licensed Neighborhood Youth Organizations. All Neighborhood Youth 
Organizations must comply with the “Rules Regulating Neighborhood Youth 
Organizations” in rule section 2.700; “General Rules Regulating Child Care Facilities” in 
rule section 2.100; and “Rules Regulating Special Activities” in rule section 2.600. 
2.703 APPLICABILITY 
The provisions of these rules and regulations shall be applicable to nonprofit 
organizations that provide programs and services to children, youth, and families 
through comprehensive wraparound supports to ensure positive growth and 
development during childhood and adolescence, and is designed to serve youth as 
young as five (5) years of age who are enrolled in kindergarten and as old as eighteen 
(18) years of age. 
2.704 DEFINITIONS

CODE OF COLORADO REGULATIONS 
8 CCR 1402-1 
Division of Early Learning, Licensing, and Administration 
 
337 
A. 
“Employee” means a paid employee of a Neighborhood Youth Organization who 
is eighteen (18) years of age or older. 
B. 
“Neighborhood Youth Organization” means a nonprofit organization that provides 
programs and services, as described in section 26.5-5-308, C.R.S., to children, 
youth, and families through comprehensive wraparound supports to ensure 
positive growth and development during childhood and adolescence, and is 
designed to serve youth as young as five (5) years of age who are enrolled in 
kindergarten and as old as eighteen (18) years of age. 
1. 
These activities must occur primarily in a facility leased by, granted access 
or use to, or owned by the Neighborhood Youth Organization. The 
activities must occur in an environment in which youth have written parent 
or guardian consent to become a youth member of the Neighborhood 
Youth Organization, and to participate in the programs and services of the 
Neighborhood Youth Organization. 
2. 
A Neighborhood Youth Organization does not include faith-based centers, 
organizations or programs operated by state or city parks or special 
districts, or departments or facilities that are currently licensed as child 
care centers as defined in rule section 2.203(B) of the “Rules Regulating 
Child Care Centers. 
C. 
"Nonprofit Organization" means an organization that is exempt from taxation 
pursuant to section 501(c)(3) of the Federal "Internal Revenue Code of 1986", 26 
U.S.C. sec. 501, as amended. 
D. 
“Volunteer” means a person who volunteers assistance to a Neighborhood Youth 
Organization and who is eighteen (18) years of age or older. 
E. 
“Youth member” means a youth who is five years of age and enrolled in 
kindergarten or who is older than five years of age and up to eighteen years of 
age whose parent or legal guardian has provided written consent for the youth to 
participate in the activities of a neighborhood youth organization.. 
F. 
A “Youth Employee” is a paid staff member of a Neighborhood Youth 
Organization who is between the ages of fourteen (14) and seventeen (17) years, 
and does not have unsupervised contact with youth. 
POLICIES AND PROCEDURES 
2.705 STATEMENT OF POLICIES AND PROCEDURES 
A. 
Each Neighborhood Youth Organization is required to have a written mission 
statement. This statement must be kept on file, updated periodically, and made 
known to employees and parent(s)/guardian(s), and must be available during
